## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: The task is to model population growth rate dP_dt as a function of time t and current population P, which is the core of single-species population dynamics. Classical models describe density-dependent growth, time-varying environments, and nonlinear feedback mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth with constant per-capita rate)
- Quadratic logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity, where c1 < 0)
- Cubic Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (strong Allee effect with critical threshold and carrying capacity)
- Power-law scaling: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (nonlinear density dependence, e.g., allometric growth when c1 ≠ 1)
- Exponential time decay: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate declines/increases exponentially due to environmental change)
- Seasonal forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * sin(c1 * t + c2) + c3 * P (periodically fluctuating per-capita growth rate)
- Constant immigration/harvest: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 + c2 * P**2 (density-independent gain or loss, such as constant harvesting or migration)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (asymmetric density dependence, growth rate varies logarithmically)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P / (c2 + c3 * t)) (logistic growth with carrying capacity changing linearly in time)
- Density-dependent threshold: dP_dt = c0 * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) * P (strong Allee effect with lower threshold and upper carrying capacity)
- Hyperbolic saturation: dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + c2 * P) (growth saturates with increasing density, analogous to Monod kinetics)
- Exponential density decay: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (growth rate decays exponentially with increasing population)
- Generalized logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**(c2 + 1) (power-law density dependence beyond quadratic)
- Rational time-density interaction: dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + c2 * t) (per-capita growth rate inversely dependent on time)
- Linear temporal decline: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * t * P (growth rate changes linearly with time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative density dependence → dP_dt decreases monotonically from positive to negative as P increases, often via a linear term with positive coefficient plus a quadratic term with negative coefficient.
- Allee effect → dP_dt shows a cubic-like shape in P: positive at intermediate P, negative at very low P and very high P, implying a positive quadratic term and negative cubic term.
- Threshold for population decline → a constant negative term in dP_dt that makes growth negative at low population sizes, indicating an extinction threshold.
- Time-dependent environmental change → explicit t in the expression for dP_dt, often as a linear or exponential modifier on the per-capita rate or carrying capacity.
- Periodic fluctuations → sinusoidal or other periodic functions of t that modulate the growth rate, reflecting seasonal breeding or resource cycles.
- Sigmoid population trajectory → dP_dt as a function of P is a concave downward parabola (quadratic), peaking at intermediate population and approaching zero at low and high P.
- Allometric or power-law growth → dP_dt ∝ P**c with c > 1 indicating accelerated growth at larger sizes, c < 1 indicating decelerated relative growth.
- Saturating density response → dP_dt approaches a maximum constant value as P becomes large, describable by rational forms like P/(1 + c*P).

The ground truth contains only polynomial terms up to \(P^3\) and a term \(P\) multiplied by an exponential; there is no dependence on \(t\), no constant term, no trigonometric, logarithmic, or rational functions.

(c_0) P^3 + (c_1 + c_2) P^2 + c_5 P + c_3 P e^{c_4 P}
\]
This matches the form of the GT precisely. The free parameters in the candidate can be assigned the corresponding GT coefficients (with \(c_4\) set to the negative of the GT exponent). The domain condition \(P \ge 0\) and the ability to zero out extra terms guarantee exact equivalence.

All other candidates either lack the required \(P e^{\text{linear } P}\) term, contain functions (sin, cos, sqrt, rational denominators) that cannot be eliminated without destroying needed structure, or include irreducible time \(t\) dependencies.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG9)

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*(c9 - exp(-c10*P))*P
Candidates evaluated: 72
Matched candidate IDs: [4, 5, 6, 30]
Matched candidates: ["P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4) + P*c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(P*c8 + 1) + c9)", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4)", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4) + P*c5", "P**3*c0/(P*c1 + c2) + P**2*c3/(P*c1 + c2) + P**2*c4/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c5/(P*c1 + c2) + P*c6*exp(P*c7)/(P*c1 + c2) + c8*exp(P*c7)/(P*c1 + c2) + c9/(P*c1 + c2)"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and determine which candidates can match it.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − exp(−0.097*P))*P
```

Let me expand this:

**Term 1:** `0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P`
= `0.17*(P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21)*P`

Let me expand `(P/1.047 − 1)*(1 − P/10.21)`:
= `P/1.047 − P²/(1.047×10.21) − 1 + P/10.21`
= `−P²/10.69 + P(1/1.047 + 1/10.21) − 1`
= `−P²/10.69 + P(0.9551 + 0.0979) − 1`
= `−P²/10.69 + 1.0530P − 1`

So Term 1 = `0.17*(−P²/10.69 + 1.053P − 1)*P`
= `0.17*(−P³/10.69 + 1.053P² − P)`
= `−0.01589P³ + 0.1790P² − 0.17P`

**Term 2:** `0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P`
= `0.17P − 0.17P²/10.21`
= `0.17P − 0.01664P²`

**Term 3:** `0.17*(1 − exp(−0.097P))*P`
= `0.17P − 0.17P*exp(−0.097P)`

**Combining all terms:**
- P³ coefficient: `−0.01589`
- P² coefficient: `0.1790 − 0.01664 = 0.16236`
- P coefficient: `−0.17 + 0.17 + 0.17 = 0.17`
- Exponential term: `−0.17*P*exp(−0.097P)`

So GT = `−0.01589P³ + 0.16236P² + 0.17P − 0.17P*exp(−0.097P)`

This can be written as:
**GT = c₀P³ + c₁P² + c₂P + c₃·P·exp(c₄·P)**

where c₄ < 0.

Now let me check each candidate against this form: **P³ + P² + P + P·exp(P)** (with appropriate constants).

### Candidate 1: `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + c3*exp(Pc4) + c5*exp(Pc6)`
Has `exp(P*c)` terms but NOT `P*exp(P*c)`. Missing the P multiplier on the exponential. **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: `P³c0 + P²c1 + P²c2 + P²c3 + Pc4 + Pc5 + c6*exp(Pc7) + c8*exp(Pc9)`
Simplifies to `P³c0 + P²(c1+c2+c3) + P(c4+c5) + c6*exp(Pc7) + c8*exp(Pc9)`. Missing P*exp term. **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: `P²c0 + Pc1 + P^c2*c3 + c4*exp(Pc5) + c6*exp(Pc7)`
Has P^c2 term. If c2=3, this gives P³. But then missing P*exp. Has exp but not P*exp. **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 4: `P³c0 + P²c1 + P²c2 + Pc3*exp(Pc4) + Pc5 + c6*sin(c7*log(Pc8+1)+c9)`
= `P³c0 + P²(c1+c2) + P*c3*exp(P*c4) + P*c5 + c6*sin(c7*log(Pc8+1)+c9)`
Has the right polynomial + P*exp terms, but also has a sin(log(...)) term. Can we set c6=0? Yes! Then it becomes `P³c0 + P²(c1+c2) + Pc5 + Pc3*exp(Pc4)`. This matches the GT form!

**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 5: `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + Pc3*exp(Pc4)`
This is exactly `P³c0 + P²c1 + Pc2 + P*c3*exp(P*c4)`. This matches the GT form perfectly!

**Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 6: `P³c0 + P²c1 + P²c2 + Pc3*exp(Pc4) + Pc5`
= `P³c0 + P²(c1+c2) + Pc5 + Pc3*exp(Pc4)`. Same as GT form.

**Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 7: `P³c0 + P²c1 + P²c2 + Pc3 + c4*sqrt(P²c5+c6)*exp(Pc7) + c8*exp(Pc9)`
Has sqrt(P²c5+c6)*exp term. Not P*exp. Could set c4=0, but then need c8*exp(Pc9) to match P*exp, which it can't. **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 8: `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2*log(Pc3+1) + c4*exp(Pc5) + c6*exp(Pc7)`
Has log term, no P³, no P*exp. **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 9: `P³c0 + Pc1 + Pc2*exp(Pc3) + c4*exp(Pc5) + c6`
= P³ + P + P*exp + exp + const. Missing P². If c4=0 and c6=0, we get P³+P+P*exp, still missing P². **[NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 10: `P²c0 + Pc1 + c2*sin(Pc3+c4) + c5*exp(Pc6) + c7*exp(Pc8)`

Pc1/(Pc2+c3) is a rational function. No P³, no P*exp. Could Pc1/(Pc2+c3) generate P² and P³? Let me check: if c2=0, Pc1/c3 = P*const. If c2≠0, Pc1/(Pc2+c3) can be expanded but gives P - const + const/(Pc2+c3). Not polynomial. Missing P³ and P*exp. **[NO MATCH]**
